.ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Missing&#95;information plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/60px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="44" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/120px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="44" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>is missing information</b> about SimpleDB, MechanicalTurk, Elastic Beanstalk, Relational Database Service, DynamoDB, CloudWatch, Simple Workflow, CloudFront, and Availability Zones.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please expand the section to include this information. Further details may exist on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Amazon_Web_Services" title="Talk:Amazon Web Services">talk page</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AWS_Simple_Icons_Storage_Amazon_EBS.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Logo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/AWS_Simple_Icons_Storage_Amazon_EBS.svg/250px-AWS_Simple_Icons_Storage_Amazon_EBS.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/AWS_Simple_Icons_Storage_Amazon_EBS.svg/330px-AWS_Simple_Icons_Storage_Amazon_EBS.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="100" /></a><figcaption>Amazon Elastic Block Store</figcaption></figure>
<p>On March 14, 2006, AWS launched <a href="/wiki/Amazon_S3" title="Amazon S3">Amazon S3</a> <a href="/wiki/Cloud_storage" title="Cloud storage">cloud storage</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pieday&#95;51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pieday-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> followed by EC2 in August 2006.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ec2l&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ec2l-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pi Corporation, a startup <a href="/wiki/Paul_Maritz" title="Paul Maritz">Paul Maritz</a> co-founded, was the first beta-user of <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Elastic_Compute_Cloud" title="Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud">EC2</a> outside of Amazon,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-hilabs&#95;21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hilabs-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> was among EC2's first enterprise customers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that year <a href="/wiki/SmugMug" title="SmugMug">SmugMug</a>, one of the early AWS adopters, attributed savings of around <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">US$</a>400,000 in storage costs to S3.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Vogels, S3 was built with 8 <a href="/wiki/Microservices" title="Microservices">microservices</a> when it launched in 2006 and had over 300 microservices by 2022.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2007, AWS announced its annual <i>Start-up Challenge</i>, a contest with prizes worth <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">$</a>100,000 for entrepreneurs and software developers in the US using AWS services such as S3 and EC2 to build their businesses.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first edition saw participation from <a href="/wiki/Justin.tv" title="Justin.tv">Justin.tv</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-schall1&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schall1-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which Amazon later acquired in 2014.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-acqtwi&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acqtwi-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ooyala" title="Ooyala">Ooyala</a>, an online media company,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> was the eventual winner.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-schall1&#95;58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schall1-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>AWS offers, as of June&#160;16,&#32;2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, two block-storage options: the EC2 Instance Store and the <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1238216509">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#0f4dc9}}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="Elastic&#95;Block&#95;Store&#95;(EBS)"></span><span class="vanchor-text">Elastic Block Store (EBS)</span></span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some Amazon EBS features that help with data management, backups, and performance tuning include:
</p>
<ul><li>EBS volume tagging to allow the user to find and filter EBS resources on the Amazon Console and CLI.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Software-level RAID arrays to enable creation of groups of EBS volumes with high performance network throughput between them, using the standard <a href="/wiki/RAID" title="RAID">RAID</a> protocol.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Additional AWS services from this period include <a href="/wiki/Amazon_SimpleDB" title="Amazon SimpleDB">SimpleDB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Mechanical_Turk" title="Amazon Mechanical Turk">Mechanical Turk</a>, <a href="/wiki/AWS_Elastic_Beanstalk" title="AWS Elastic Beanstalk">Elastic Beanstalk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Relational_Database_Service" title="Amazon Relational Database Service">Relational Database Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_DynamoDB" title="Amazon DynamoDB">DynamoDB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Elastic_Compute_Cloud#Amazon_CloudWatch" title="Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud">CloudWatch</a>, Simple Workflow, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_CloudFront" title="Amazon CloudFront">CloudFront</a>, and Availability Zones.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Growth_(2010–2015)"><span id="Growth_.282010.E2.80.932015.29"></span>Growth (2010–2015)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Growth (2010–2015)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AWSSummit2013NYC2.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/AWSSummit2013NYC2.JPG/250px-AWSSummit2013NYC2.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/AWSSummit2013NYC2.JPG/500px-AWSSummit2013NYC2.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>AWS Summit 2013 event in NYC</figcaption></figure>
<p>In November 2010, it was reported that all of Amazon.com's retail sites had migrated to AWS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Prior to 2012, AWS was considered a part of Amazon.com and so its revenue was not delineated in Amazon financial statements. In that year industry watchers for the first time estimated AWS revenue to be over $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On November 27, 2012, AWS hosted its first major annual conference, <i>re:Invent</i> with a focus on AWS's partners and ecosystem,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with over 150 sessions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-freinventblog&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freinventblog-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The three-day event was held in Las Vegas because of its relatively cheaper connectivity with locations across the United States and the rest of the world.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Andy Jassy and Werner Vogels presented keynotes, with Jeff Bezos joining Vogels for a fireside chat.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-net1&#95;69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-net1-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AWS opened early registrations at  <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">US$</a>1,099 per head for their customers<sup id="cite&#95;ref-freinventblog&#95;67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freinventblog-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> from over 190 countries.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On stage with Andy Jassy at the event which saw around 6000 attendees, <a href="/wiki/Reed_Hastings" title="Reed Hastings">Reed Hastings</a>, CEO at <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>, announced plans to migrate 100% of Netflix's infrastructure to AWS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-net1&#95;69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-net1-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>To support industry-wide training and skills standardization, AWS began offering a certification program for computer engineers, on April 30, 2013, to highlight expertise in cloud computing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that year, in October, AWS launched <i>Activate</i>, a program for start-ups worldwide to leverage AWS credits, third-party integrations, and free access to AWS experts to help build their business.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, AWS launched its partner network, AWS Partner Network (APN), which is focused on helping AWS-based companies grow and scale the success of their business with close collaboration and best practices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2015, Amazon Web Services acquired <a href="/wiki/Annapurna_Labs" title="Annapurna Labs">Annapurna Labs</a>, an Israel-based microelectronics company for a reported US$350–370M.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-reut&#95;Amaz&#95;75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut_Amaz-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-extr&#95;Amaz&#95;76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extr_Amaz-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2015, Amazon.com reported AWS was profitable, with sales of $1.57 billion in the first quarter of the year and $265 million of operating income. Founder <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a> described it as a fast-growing $5 billion business; analysts described it as "surprisingly more profitable than forecast".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October, Amazon.com said in its Q3 earnings report that AWS's operating income was $521 million, with operating margins at 25 percent. AWS's 2015 Q3 revenue was $2.1 billion, a 78% increase from 2014's Q3 revenue of $1.17 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 2015 Q4 revenue for the AWS segment increased 69.5% y/y to $2.4 billion with a 28.5% operating margin, giving AWS a $9.6 billion run rate. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a> estimated that AWS customers are deploying 10x more infrastructure on AWS than the combined adoption of the next 14 providers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Since_2016">Since 2016</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Since 2016"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2016 Q1, revenue was $2.57 billion with net income of $604 million, a 64% increase over 2015 Q1 that resulted in AWS being more profitable than Amazon's North American retail business for the first time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Jassy was thereafter promoted to CEO of the division.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-CEO&#95;Andy&#95;Jassy&#95;81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEO_Andy_Jassy-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Around the same time, Amazon experienced a 42% rise in stock value as a result of increased earnings, of which AWS contributed 56% to corporate profits.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>AWS had $17.46 billion in annual revenue in 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto1&#95;83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the end of 2020, the number had grown to <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">$</a>46 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2020sales&#95;84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020sales-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Reflecting the success of AWS, Jassy's annual compensation in 2017 hit nearly $36 million.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018, Amazon launched a unified <a href="/wiki/Autoscaling" title="Autoscaling">autoscaling</a> service on AWS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This new service unifies and builds on AWS existing, service-specific, scaling features like EC2 Auto Scaling groups, that was launched in August 2006.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2018, AWS announced customized ARM cores for use in its servers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also in November 2018, AWS created ground stations to communicate with customers' satellites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, AWS reported 37% yearly growth and accounted for 12% of Amazon's revenue (up from 11% in 2018).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2021, AWS reported 32% yearly growth and accounted for 32% of $41.8 billion cloud market in Q1 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2022, AWS joined the <a href="/wiki/MACH_Alliance" title="MACH Alliance">MACH Alliance</a>, a non-profit enterprise technology advocacy group.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022, it was reported that in 2019 Capital One had not secured their AWS resources properly, and was subject to a data breach by a former AWS employee. The employee was convicted of hacking into the company's cloud servers to steal customer data and use computer power to mine cryptocurrency. The ex-employee was able to download the personal information of more than 100 million Capital One customers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2022, AWS announced they had launched the AWS Snowcone, a small computing device, to the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Axiom_Mission_1" title="Axiom Mission 1">Axiom Mission 1</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2023, AWS announced it would become AI startup <a href="/wiki/Anthropic" title="Anthropic">Anthropic</a>'s primary cloud provider. Amazon has committed to investing up to $4 billion in Anthropic and will have a minority ownership position in the company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AWS also announced the GA of <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Bedrock" title="Amazon Bedrock">Amazon Bedrock</a>, a fully managed service that makes foundation models (FMs) from leading AI companies available through a single application programming interface (API)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2024, AWS announced a new service called Deadline Cloud, which lets customers set up, deploy and scale up graphics and visual effects rendering pipelines on AWS cloud infrastructure.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2024, AWS announced Amazon Nova, its own family of <a href="/wiki/Foundation_model" title="Foundation model">foundation models</a>. These models, offered through Amazon Bedrock, are designed for various tasks including content generation, video understanding, and building agentic applications. They are available in six different sizes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the end of 2024, AWS announced Project Rainier, a massive one-of-a-kind machine "designed to usher in the next generation of AI."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Customer_base">Customer base</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Customer base"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In October 2013, AWS was awarded a $600M contract with the <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>By 2019, it was reported that more than 80% of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>'s listed <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> companies used AWS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In August 2019, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">U.S. Navy</a> said it moved 72,000 users from six commands to an AWS cloud system as a first step toward pushing all of its data and analytics onto the cloud.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2021, Amazon announced that it would suspend <a href="/wiki/Parler" title="Parler">Parler</a> from Amazon Web Services, stating Parler hosted “violent content” that violates its terms of service.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later in 2021, <a href="/wiki/Dish_Network" title="Dish Network">DISH Network</a> announced it would develop and launch its <a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">5G</a> network on AWS.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was also reported that spy agencies and government departments in the UK, such as <a href="/wiki/GCHQ" title="GCHQ">GCHQ</a>, <a href="/wiki/MI5" title="MI5">MI5</a>, <a href="/wiki/MI6" title="MI6">MI6</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a>, contracted AWS to host their classified materials.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2022, Amazon shared a $9 billion contract from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> for cloud computing with Google, Microsoft, and Oracle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>AWS won a $581 million contract from the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Air Force">U.S. Air Force</a> in January 2026 to provide cloud services and specific Amazon data centers as part of the Cloud One Program, the Air Force's enterprise cloud environment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Multiple financial services firms have shifted to AWS in some form.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Notable customers include <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2012">Obama presidential campaign of 2012</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Significant_service_outages">Significant service outages</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Significant service outages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Amazon_Web_Services#Outages" title="Timeline of Amazon Web Services">Timeline of Amazon Web Services §&#160;Outages</a></div>
<ul><li>On April 20, 2011, AWS suffered a major outage. Parts of the Elastic Block Store service became "stuck" and could not fulfill read/write requests. It took at least two days for the service to be fully restored.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On June 29, 2012, several websites that rely on Amazon Web Services were taken offline due to <a href="/wiki/June_2012_North_American_derecho" title="June 2012 North American derecho">a severe storm</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a>, where AWS's largest data center cluster is located.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On October 22, 2012, a major outage occurred, affecting many sites including <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foursquare_City_Guide" title="Foursquare City Guide">Foursquare</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pinterest" title="Pinterest">Pinterest</a>. The cause was a memory leak bug in an operational data collection agent.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On December 24, 2012, AWS suffered another outage causing websites such as <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> to be unavailable for customers in the Northeastern United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AWS cited their <a href="/wiki/Elastic_Load_Balancing" class="mw-redirect" title="Elastic Load Balancing">Elastic Load Balancing</a> service as the cause.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On February 28, 2017, AWS experienced a massive outage of S3 services in its Northern Virginia region. A majority of websites that relied on AWS S3 either hung or stalled, and Amazon reported within five hours that AWS was fully online again.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> No data has been reported to have been lost due to the outage. The outage was caused by a <a href="/wiki/Human_error" title="Human error">human error</a> made while <a href="/wiki/Debugging" title="Debugging">debugging</a>, that resulted in removing more server capacity than intended, which caused a domino effect of outages.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On November 25, 2020, AWS experienced several hours of outage on the Kinesis service in North Virginia (US-East-1) region. Other services relying on Kinesis were also affected.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On December 7, 2021, an outage mainly affected the Eastern United States, disrupting delivery service and streaming.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On October 20, 2025, AWS suffered a major outage, resulting in platforms including <a href="/wiki/Duolingo" title="Duolingo">Duolingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snapchat" title="Snapchat">Snapchat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canva" title="Canva">Canva</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instructure" title="Instructure">Canvas</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coinbase" title="Coinbase">Coinbase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roblox" title="Roblox">Roblox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fortnite" title="Fortnite">Fortnite</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> being down.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Availability_and_topology">Availability and topology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Availability and topology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>As of October&#160;2025,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> AWS has distinct operations in 38 geographical "regions":<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GlobalInfrastructure&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalInfrastructure-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> nine in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, two in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, nine in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, four in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, one in Africa, thirteen in the <a href="/wiki/Asia%E2%80%93Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia–Pacific">Asia–Pacific</a>, and three in Australia and New Zealand.
</p><p>Most AWS regions are enabled by default for AWS accounts. Regions introduced after 20 March 2019 are considered to be <i>opt-in</i> regions, requiring a user to explicitly enable them in order for the region to be usable in the account. For opt-in regions, Identity and Access Management (IAM) resources such as users and roles are only propagated to the regions that are enabled.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Each region is wholly contained within a single country and all of its data and services stay within the designated region.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-AWSagreement&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWSagreement-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Each region has multiple "Availability Zones",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GlobalInfrastructure&#95;10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalInfrastructure-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which consist of one or more discrete <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data centers</a>, each with <a href="/wiki/Emergency_power_system" title="Emergency power system">redundant power</a>, networking, and connectivity, housed in separate facilities. Availability Zones do not automatically provide additional scalability or redundancy within a region, since they are intentionally isolated from each other to prevent <a href="/wiki/Network_outage" class="mw-redirect" title="Network outage">outages</a> from spreading between zones. Several services can operate across Availability Zones (e.g., S3, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_DynamoDB" title="Amazon DynamoDB">DynamoDB</a>) while others can be configured to replicate across zones to spread demand and avoid <a href="/wiki/Downtime" title="Downtime">downtime</a> from failures.
</p><p>As of December&#160;2014,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Amazon Web Services operated an estimated 1.4 million servers across 11 regions and 28 availability zones.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The global network of AWS Edge locations consists of over 700 points of presence worldwide, including locations in North America, Europe, Asia, Australia and New Zealand, Africa, and South America.The AWS Cloud spans 120 Availability Zones within 38 Geographic Regions, with announced plans for 10 more Availability Zones and 3 more AWS Regions in the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia, Chile, and the AWS European Sovereign Cloud.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GlobalInfrastructure&#95;10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalInfrastructure-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of March&#160;2024,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> AWS had announced the planned launch of six additional regions in Malaysia, Mexico, New Zealand, Thailand, Saudi Arabia, and the European Union.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GlobalInfrastructure&#95;10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalInfrastructure-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In mid March 2023, Amazon Web Services signed a cooperation agreement with the New Zealand Government to build large data centers in New Zealand.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Pop-up_lofts">Pop-up lofts</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pop-up lofts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_Web_Services_(AWS)_Loft_-_NYC_(48129118457).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Amazon_Web_Services_%28AWS%29_Loft_-_NYC_%2848129118457%29.jpg/250px-Amazon_Web_Services_%28AWS%29_Loft_-_NYC_%2848129118457%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="187" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Amazon_Web_Services_%28AWS%29_Loft_-_NYC_%2848129118457%29.jpg/500px-Amazon_Web_Services_%28AWS%29_Loft_-_NYC_%2848129118457%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3927" data-file-height="2945" /></a><figcaption>AWS Loft in <a href="/wiki/SoHo" class="mw-redirect" title="SoHo">SoHo</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>AWS also has "pop-up lofts" in different locations around the world.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These market AWS to entrepreneurs and startups in different tech industries in a physical location. Visitors can work or relax inside the loft, or learn more about what they can do with AWS. In June 2014, AWS opened their first temporary pop-up loft in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2015 they expanded to New York City,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in September 2015 expanded to Berlin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AWS opened its fourth location, in Tel Aviv from March 1, 2016, to March 22, 2016.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A pop-up loft was open in London from September 10 to October 29, 2015.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The pop-up lofts in New York<sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and San Francisco<sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are indefinitely<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2026)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> closed due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> while Tokyo has remained open in a limited capacity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Charitable_work">Charitable work</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Charitable work"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2017, AWS launched AWS re/Start in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> to help young adults and military veterans retrain in technology-related skills.  In partnership with the <a href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince&#39;s Trust">Prince's Trust</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MoD), AWS will help to provide re-training opportunities for young people from disadvantaged backgrounds and former military personnel. AWS is working alongside a number of partner companies including Cloudreach, <a href="/wiki/Sage_Group" title="Sage Group">Sage Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/EDF_Energy" title="EDF Energy">EDF Energy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tesco_Bank" title="Tesco Bank">Tesco Bank</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2022, AWS announced that the organization had committed more than $30 million over three years to early-stage start-ups led by Black, Latino, LGBTQIA+, and women founders as part of its AWS impact Accelerator. The Initiative offers qualifying start-ups up to $225,000 in cash, credits, extensive training, mentoring, technical guidance and includes up to $100,000 in AWS service credits.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Environmental_footprint">Environmental footprint</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Environmental footprint"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2014, AWS claimed its aim was to achieve <a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% renewable energy</a> usage in the future.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In the United States, AWS's partnerships with renewable energy providers include Community Energy of Virginia, to support the US East region;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-burt2015&#95;145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burt2015-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pattern Development, in January 2015, to construct and operate Amazon <a href="/wiki/Fowler_Ridge_Wind_Farm" title="Fowler Ridge Wind Farm">Wind Farm Fowler Ridge</a>;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Avangrid" title="Avangrid">Iberdrola Renewables</a>, LLC, in July 2015, to construct and operate Amazon Wind Farm US East; <a href="/wiki/EDP_Renewables_North_America" title="EDP Renewables North America">EDP Renewables North America</a>, in November 2015, to construct and operate Amazon Wind Farm US Central;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>, to apply battery storage technology to address power needs in the US West (Northern California) region.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-burt2015&#95;145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burt2015-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> assessed major tech companies—including cloud services providers like AWS, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salesforce" title="Salesforce">Salesforce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rackspace" class="mw-redirect" title="Rackspace">Rackspace</a>—based on their level of "clean energy" usage. Greenpeace evaluated companies on their mix of renewable-energy sources; transparency; renewable-energy commitment and policies; energy efficiency and greenhouse-gas mitigation; renewable-energy procurement; and advocacy. The group gave AWS an overall "C" grade. Greenpeace credited AWS for its advances toward greener computing in recent years and its plans to launch multiple wind and solar farms across the United States. The organization stated that Amazon is opaque about its <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2021, AWS joined an industry pledge to achieve <a href="/wiki/Carbon_neutrality" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon neutrality">climate neutrality</a> of data centers by 2030, the <a href="/wiki/Climate_Neutral_Data_Centre_Pact" title="Climate Neutral Data Centre Pact">Climate Neutral Data Centre Pact</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2023, Amazon as a whole is the largest corporate purchaser of renewable energy in the world, a position it has held since 2020, and has a global portfolio of over 20 GW of renewable energy capacity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2022, 90% of all Amazon operations, including data centers, were powered by renewables.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2024, AWS paid $650 million for a data center<sup id="cite&#95;ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> at the 2.5 GW <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_Steam_Electric_Station" title="Susquehanna Steam Electric Station">Susquehanna nuclear power plant</a>, connected at 300 MW. In 2025, AWS signed an $18 billion <a href="/wiki/Power_purchase_agreement" title="Power purchase agreement">power purchase agreement</a> with the station for 840—1,200 MW in 2029 and 1,680—1,920 MW in 2032, continuing to 2042. The power increase depends on Amazon's expansion of the data center.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-pat&#95;153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pat-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Denaturalization_protest">Denaturalization protest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Denaturalization protest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>US <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Homeland_Security" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> has employed the software ATLAS, which runs on Amazon Cloud. It scanned more than 16.5 million records of naturalized Americans and flagged approximately 124,000 of them for manual analysis and review by <a href="/wiki/USCIS" class="mw-redirect" title="USCIS">USCIS</a> officers regarding <a href="/wiki/Denaturalization" title="Denaturalization">denaturalization</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some of the scanned data came from the <a href="/wiki/Terrorist_Screening_Database" title="Terrorist Screening Database">Terrorist Screening Database</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Crime_Information_Center" title="National Crime Information Center">National Crime Information Center</a>. The algorithm and the criteria for the algorithm were secret. Amazon faced protests from its own employees and activists for the anti-migrant collaboration with authorities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Israeli–Palestinian_conflict"><span id="Israeli.E2.80.93Palestinian_conflict"></span>Israeli–Palestinian conflict</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Israeli–Palestinian conflict"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a></div>
<p>The contract for <a href="/wiki/Project_Nimbus" title="Project Nimbus">Project Nimbus</a> drew rebuke and condemnation from the companies' shareholders as well as their employees, over concerns that the project would lead to abuses of <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians'</a> human rights in the context of the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Israeli occupation of the West Bank">occupation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli–Palestinian conflict">Israeli–Palestinian conflict</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-anon-workers&#95;159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anon-workers-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Specifically, they voice concern over how the technology will enable further <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance" title="Mass surveillance">surveillance</a> of Palestinians and unlawful <a href="/wiki/Data_collection" title="Data collection">data collection</a> on them as well as facilitate the expansion of Israel's <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">illegal settlements</a> on Palestinian land.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-anon-workers&#95;159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anon-workers-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A government procurement document featuring 'obligatory customers' of Nimbus, including "two of Israel’s leading state-owned weapons manufacturers" <a href="/wiki/Israel_Aerospace_Industries" title="Israel Aerospace Industries">Israel Aerospace Industries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Advanced_Defense_Systems" title="Rafael Advanced Defense Systems">Rafael Advanced Defense Systems</a>, was published in 2021 with periodic updates since (up to Oct 2023).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Work_with_sanctioned_companies">Work with sanctioned companies</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Work with sanctioned companies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>AWS has been noted to work with Chinese companies under varying degrees of <a href="/wiki/United_States_sanctions_against_China" title="United States sanctions against China">U.S. government sanctions</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Hikvision" title="Hikvision">Hikvision</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dahua_Technology" title="Dahua Technology">Dahua Technology</a>, which have been accused to enabling <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance_in_China" title="Mass surveillance in China">mass surveillance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_China" title="Human rights in China">human rights abuses in China</a> and elsewhere.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Security_incidents">Security incidents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Security incidents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Amazon_Q_Developer_Extension_supply-chain_vulnerability_(2025)"><span id="Amazon_Q_Developer_Extension_supply-chain_vulnerability_.282025.29"></span>Amazon Q Developer Extension supply-chain vulnerability (2025)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Amazon Q Developer Extension supply-chain vulnerability (2025)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In July 2025, a security researcher disclosed a supply-chain vulnerability in the Amazon Q Developer Extension (version 1.84) for Visual Studio Code.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The issue involved a malicious pull request to the project's GitHub repository, which introduced a prompt instructing the AI assistant to delete local files and AWS resources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> AWS acknowledged the issue in Security Bulletin AWS‑2025‑015 and released version 1.85 to remove the injected prompt. The company stated that no customer systems or data were affected.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, critics including Corey Quinn, writing in Last Week in AWS, questioned the transparency of the response, noting the absence of a changelog entry, a CVE assignment, or a public statement beyond the bulletin.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Log4Shell_Hot_Patch_vulnerability">Log4Shell Hot Patch vulnerability</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Log4Shell Hot Patch vulnerability"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In response to the <a href="/wiki/Log4Shell" title="Log4Shell">Log4Shell vulnerability</a>, AWS released hot patch solutions to mitigate risks in Java applications across various environments, including standalone servers, Kubernetes clusters, and Elastic Container Service (ECS). These patches were designed for both AWS and non-AWS environments. However, researchers from Unit 42 at <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto_Networks" title="Palo Alto Networks">Palo Alto Networks</a> identified critical security flaws in these patches that could be exploited for container escape and privilege escalation, potentially granting attackers unauthorized root-level access to the host system. AWS addressed these vulnerabilities by releasing updated patches on April 19, 2022. Users who deployed the initial patches were advised to upgrade to the latest versions to mitigate security risks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Application_Load_Balancer_security_issue">Application Load Balancer security issue</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Application Load Balancer security issue"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In April 2024, security researchers from Miggo security identified a configuration vulnerability in AWS Application Load Balancer (ALB) that could allow attackers to bypass access controls and compromise web applications. The issue stemmed from how some users configured ALB's authentication handoff to third-party services, potentially enabling unauthorized access to application data. On July 11, 2024, AWS confirmed the issue affecting its customers, and on July 19, 2024, AWS updated its documentation accordingly to recommend more secure implementation practices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Issues">Issues</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Issues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1305433154" /><table class="box-Page&#95;numbers&#95;needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Text_document_with_page_number_icon.svg/40px-Text_document_with_page_number_icon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Text_document_with_page_number_icon.svg/60px-Text_document_with_page_number_icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Text_document_with_page_number_icon.svg/120px-Text_document_with_page_number_icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section cites its sources <b>but does not provide <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITEHOW" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:CITEHOW">page references</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by providing page numbers for existing citations.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2025</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Some AWS customers have complained about receiving unexpectedly large bills, commonly referred to as "surprise bills." This can occur due to various reasons, including but not limited to misconfigurations, security breaches, complex pricing—especially when multiple AWS services are used together—and unexpected data transfer charges.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Pricing">Pricing</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Pricing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Data_transfer_charges">Data transfer charges</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon_Web_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Data transfer charges"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>AWS applies charges for data transferred both between Availability Zones within the same region (inter-AZ) and across different geographic regions (inter-region). The pricing structure is influenced by several factors, including the source and destination of the data, the specific AWS services in use, and the underlying networking architecture.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Various services implement different data transfer models, and the choice of communication method—such as VPC Peering,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Transit Gateway,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or AWS PrivateLink<sup id="cite&#95;ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>—can also affect the overall cost.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
